MR. SWAIN MAKES OPEN CONFESSION.
I have been an architect for a period of about thirty
years, and I am sufficiently egotistical to believe that I know
my business fairly well. If that were not the case I would
not be permitted to hold my present position. All of the
changes that have been made in the original plans and speci
fications for the ferry building have been made with my con
sent and have received my official approval. I did approve
of the substitution of pine for oak In the Interior finish of the
building, and It was with my approval that the Commissioners
paid the contractors $2995 more for putting in pine than
would have been paid them for putting In oak.
I approved of permitting the contractors to omit building
six floors in the tower, they In return agreeing to deduct $119
from the amount of their contract price. Later I approved of
allowing them $310 for building one of the discarded floors.
I think I have done my duty. â From an interview -with â¢
Architect Swain.

"I approved of the estimates allow

for laying the pine floors in the offices
an the ground float of the ferry build
ing," he said yesterday, "and that is
all I will say about the matter. I am
willing to stand by my acts in this and
all other matters. I decline to give any
more information on this or any other
point pertaining to the construction of
the ferry building."
Among other things that Mr. Swain
declined to discuss was the method by

inal plans and specifications, and the

Other and important reductions were
made in this amended contract. Among
them were: Omitting all coverings on
lavatories, making windows stationary
and omitting openings to same, using
16 ounce glass in lights of 18 inches
square or less, reductions in details of
doors, transoms, inside finish and hard
ware. In the architect's memorandum
of moneys paid to Bateman Bros, it is
shown that 3-16 corrugated glass was
substituted for 16 ounce sheet glass. The
memorandum shows that the contrac
tor received for these reductions the
sum of $551 25. From such data as is
obtainable it is shown that the firm of
Bateman Bros, was paid a total of
$9115 70 for extras. This amount, added
to the amount of their original con
tract $48,400, makes a total of $57,515.
For this money the State gets pine in
stead of oak partitions on the first and
second stories, and gets nothing at all
on the mezzanine floor where thirty
flve rooms were to be finished in oak.
This item of woodwork is only one of
the many jobs that are being brought
to the surface by the investigation that
is being made of the construction of the
ferry depot building and those who are
responsible for what is being done in
connection with the work. It will serve
as an illustration to show how the
State's money is being expended.
FUNERAL OF MISS SCHXTLTZ.
Last Sad and Touching Tribute at
the Home of the Parents. ,
As Priscilla "will live forever in the
hearts of those who follow puritanical
history, so will live in the memory of the
musical people of this city Miss Florence
Muriel Schultz. who personated the pil
grim maiden at the California Theater
during the Columbia Pageant. No monu
ment will be erected to the memory of the
beautiful and accomplished daughter of
Professor and Mrs. Martin Schultz It
will be found in the hearts of those that
knew and loved her. â¢
The funeral services were held at 10
o'clock yesterday morning at the resi
dence ;of the grief stricken parents, 221
Pierce street. Loving relatives and
friends had sent most j beautiful floral
tributes, two very exquisite pieces being
from Miss Schultz's classmates of the
Crocker School. Rev. C. R. Brown of the
First Congregational Church of Oakland
officiated at the services, and musical
selections were rendered by Messrs. Sam
Mayer Jones, Fleming and Ogilvie. Atier
the services at the residence the remains
â ^re sent to Odd Fellows Cemetery for
cremation.

Libel Against the Martha Davis.
Assistant United States Attorney Knlgnt
yesterday filed in the United States Dsis
trict Court a libel against the bark Mar
tha Davis for $2000, the alleged value of
damages inflicted upon the Government
steamer Patterson on March 10 by the
Davis colliding with the steamer.
